  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0a9519f0-2d73-4a2e-b474-b5c55f63d325'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer6971670968625001667">I read the last few chapters as a reminder because I already have the 9th volume. The only thing that stands out is that Light Yagami has become a pansy. That's right, I said it! Ever since what happened with L in the last volume, and the years that have passed, Light has gotten soft and I don't like it one bit.   <span id="freeText6971670968625001667" style="display:none">I read the last few chapters as a reminder because I already have the 9th volume. The only thing that stands out is that Light Yagami has become a pansy. That's right, I said it! Ever since what happened with L in the last volume, and the years that have passed, Light has gotten soft and I don't like it one bit. In this volume, Light now has concerns for the well-being of his family and actually <i>doesn't</i> want to put them at risk. Really?! Wasn't it in the first or second volume that Light was willing to sacrifice his family? Damn it, Light. Go back to being a sociopath! And then I'm confused as to who Light is supposed to be. There's so much that he says, it gets me off track. I'm only continuing to read this because 1) my sister says that the anime ending was...thought provoking. and 2) i really wanna know what happens to somehow who uses the Death Note. they can neither go to heaven or hell. Hmm.</span>

<div id="review_756591384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756591384" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756591384?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=evul-people-are-evul">evul-people-are-evul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756591384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2874115729458031695"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>-Light was a stone cold bastard. He didn't have any loving or kind feelings whatsoever, at least early in the series he seemed to care for his family and genuinely wanted to make the world a better place. He was no longer like that, he was willing to kill Sayu, his dad, and anyone else if they got in the way of his goal to create a new world he could control. <br/>Also, the fact he was living with Misa for years but still hadn't developed any feelings for her showed how inhuman he was, he wa</span>
  <span id="freeText2874115729458031695" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />-Light was a stone cold bastard. He didn't have any loving or kind feelings whatsoever, at least early in the series he seemed to care for his family and genuinely wanted to make the world a better place. He was no longer like that, he was willing to kill Sayu, his dad, and anyone else if they got in the way of his goal to create a new world he could control. <br />Also, the fact he was living with Misa for years but still hadn't developed any feelings for her showed how inhuman he was, he was totally fine with using her and then killing her if it suited his purpose. <br />He had no redeeming qualities whatsoever or any human-ness about him, it made him come across as a caricature, at least he had some depth before. I really hope he gets killed soon.<br /><br />-The new dynamics with Light having to stay one step ahead of N and Mello was kind of interesting. But I wasn't all that impressed with how much Mello/Near reminded me of L. Even though they were just as, if not more, intelligent and logical than L, they still seemed like poor versions of him. Maybe, they'll develop and stand out on their own in later volumes.<br /><br />-Notes: Light's sister (Sayu) was kidnapped by a group who wanted the Death Note. Light had two new opponents, both of them were trained to be L's successors: Near/N was promoted as the new L and was working with the FBI. And Mello joined the Mafia when Near/N became the new L.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2874115729458031695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And then lil sis Sayu, whose brother is mercilessly contemplating killing her off, just so he can have an easier time as a brutal mass murderer. Poor guy. All he wants is his magical murder weapon back, is that so much to ask?</span>

<div id="review_718303633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718303633" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12248943-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499990463p2/12248943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718303633?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/12248943-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-books-have-good-covers">good-books-have-good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-graphic-novels">good-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718303633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11112304277130880518">And, at last, Death Note is good again.<br/><br/>It'll sound weird to a lot of fans that I'm saying that. A lot of fans hate this arc - from this volume until volume 12, things went downhill for a lot of people. And I just don't get that, to be honest. Yes, I miss L, just like everybody else. But the fact that one character died doesn't suddenly make the series bad. And moreover, the memoryless Light arc was so terrible that this is a welcome break. That arc was filled with plotholes, it was thematically </span>
  <span id="freeText11112304277130880518" style="display:none">And, at last, Death Note is good again.<br><br>It'll sound weird to a lot of fans that I'm saying that. A lot of fans hate this arc - from this volume until volume 12, things went downhill for a lot of people. And I just don't get that, to be honest. Yes, I miss L, just like everybody else. But the fact that one character died doesn't suddenly make the series bad. And moreover, the memoryless Light arc was so terrible that this is a welcome break. That arc was filled with plotholes, it was thematically boring, and it was predictable. This was a return to form for Death Note - finally, things are interesting and suspenseful again.<br><br>Things are so good, the misogyny can barely even harsh my mellow. Yes, it pisses me off that Misa is happy under Light's blatant abuse, happy to be his subordinate, happy to be manipulated. But I'm just so happy that Ohba got the series back on track that I barely even care. Light's sister being kidnapped was one of the most suspenseful arcs here, because it was genuinely difficult to tell what Light would do, something we haven't seen in ages. And it's cool to see that he <i>isn't actually a psychopath</i>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Light would've killed anyone else to get the notebook back, but he spared his sister. He doesn't feel comfortable going quite that far. His mind can be changed, and he does have sympathy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's pretty subtle, but it's one of the most significant parts of the series, if you ask me.<br><br>Things are more complicated here than at any other point in the series. Before, it had been Kira vs. L, then L vs. Yotsuba. Now, it's Kira vs. the Japanese Police Force vs. the SPK vs. the Mafia. Not to mention Shinigami interference. Each group is fairly self-interested, and each group has different goals. A lot of fans claim that things get confusing in this arc, and I do see where they're coming from. But if you can keep up with it - and it's not that hard, if you're willing to give it all your mental attention - it's very engaging. The gambits pile on top of each other, and Ohba brings it together beautifully.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419182232i/13007840._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, other than the misogyny, I'm finding very little to complain about. There are only four volumes left, and I really don't want this series to end.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11112304277130880518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_438484964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438484964" />
    <a title="Dong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12787902-dong"><img alt="Dong" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438484964?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dong" href="/user/show/12787902-dong">Dong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438484964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9633624047487125908">Death Note, #8 is written by Tsugumi Ohba and drawn by Takeshi Obata and is 200 pages long. The genre of the story is mystery and also realistic modern time science fiction.<br/><br/>The book is based on a notebook, called the Death Note, that allows a person to "kill" another person just by writing the full name of the person and thinking of an image of them. This notebook solely belongs to the Death Gods, or "Shinigamis", but one day, a death god named Ryuk is bored and throws the book to the human worl</span>
  <span id="freeText9633624047487125908" style="display:none">Death Note, #8 is written by Tsugumi Ohba and drawn by Takeshi Obata and is 200 pages long. The genre of the story is mystery and also realistic modern time science fiction.<br /><br />The book is based on a notebook, called the Death Note, that allows a person to "kill" another person just by writing the full name of the person and thinking of an image of them. This notebook solely belongs to the Death Gods, or "Shinigamis", but one day, a death god named Ryuk is bored and throws the book to the human world. Light Yagami, a straight-A regular high-school student, picks up the book and find out what the book does. Because he romanticizes a perfect world, he believes that using this notebook to kill criminals will be able to purify the world. L, a mysterious genius who work and specialize in solving worldwide crimes, fights against Yagami, or "Kira", but after several conflicts, L eventually loses and gets killed by Light, leaving Light unstoppable.<br /><br />In this volume, the two successors of L is introduced: Near and Mello. Near was working with the United Staes government, in the attempt to catch Kira, but, on the other hand, Mello is trying to gain the notebook that Light possessed. Little does he know that Light actually gains another Notebook. Light actually gains the guts to join the anti-Kira Japanese police division where his father is. His idea was to eliminate any suspicion by joining the anti-Kira. Mello gets hold of Light's sister and the direct (or Light's father) decides to trade the notebook that the police gains from the investigation and succeeds in getting in touch with Mello. <br /><br />Because I enjoyed the previous chapter quite deeply, I was really excited when I started this book. However, I am really disappointed with the new plot. Though I am content that there is a sequel, I just think that the new one does not match with the preceding one and fails to explore more deeply. However, I do want to see how the book concludes and rather Light finishes his quest to a perfect world or fails and meets his demise by the new L's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9633624047487125908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('338k8a4oqXcQAYfrCWm228+HiB0sZK9XkDwcniiLkRZ1u+FeNrYhDsjVLXybeZE9ezgnXyTSwZllm984HoVB0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MhxsnKlmd0Yaz9rogcJE6SEecmd3ihRVdAhPfQqL0BqY2KkzMfj/P8IbcH8T0mMPlaHdJX88epuBr4zbPIUA3Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5335273548243600000">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText5335273548243600000" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
